Illustrated Encyclopedia [0m(London: Near Fine, 1995) are essential reference works. Three valuable histories of science fiction are

the Twentieth Century [0m(Oxford: Oxford University Press, 1994); and Brian Stablefordโs [3mThe Sociology of Science Fiction [0m(San 
Bernardino: Borgo Press, 2007). Among numerous other useful reference works are M. Keith Booker and Anne-Marie Thomas (eds.), [3mThe 
Science Fiction Handbook [0m(Malden, MA, and Oxford: Wiley-Blackwell, 2009); Mark Bould et al. (eds.), [3mThe Routledge Companion to

Science Fiction [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 2003); and David Seed (ed.), [3mA Companion to Science Fiction [0m(Oxford: 
Blackwell, 2005). Joanna Russโs comments on science fiction can be found in [3mThe Country You Have Never Seen [0m(Liverpool: Liverpool 
University Press, 2007). Istvan Csicsery-Ronay, [3mThe Seven Beauties of Science Fiction [0m(Middletown, CT: Wesleyan University Press, 
2008) presents a series of far-reaching essays on SF. Phil Hardyโs [3mOverlook Film Encyclopedia [0m(New York: Overlook Press, 1995) is 
a valuable reference work.

[1mุงููุตู ุงูุฑุงุจุน: ุงููุฏู ุงููุงุถูุฉ (ููุชูุจูุง) ูุงููุฏู ุงููุงุณุฏุฉ (ุฏูุณุชูุจูุง) [0m

Darko Suvin, [3mPositions and Presuppositions in Science Fiction [0m(London: Macmillan, 1988) contains his definition of utopias. His

House, 1975), and [3mMore Women of Wonder: Science Fiction Novelettes by Women about Women [0m(New York: Vintage, 1976) were pioneering

IN: Indiana University Press, 1995), and Ursula Le Guinโs main comments on science fiction are collected in [3mThe Language of the

received image of womenโs presence in science fiction 1926โ65, arguing that it was far more extensive than widely supposed. Michel 
Foucaultโs 1967 paper โOf Other Spacesโ is available at http://foucault.info/documents/heteroTopia/foucault.heteroTopia.en.html 
(accessed 10 January 2011).

H. G. Wells, [3mThe Discovery of the Future [0m(London: Polytechnic of North London Press, 1989) reprints his famous essay. John

Nicholas Ruddick, [3mThe Fire in the Stone [0m(Middletown, CT: Wesleyan University Press, 2009) surveys the mainly Darwinian tradition

1987) assembles essays on how SF confronts the future; and Fredric Jameson, [3mArchaeologies of the Future [0m(London and New York: 
Verso, 2005) presents a sophisticated Marxist interpretation of utopian and other SF. W. Warren Wagar, [3mTerminal Visions [0m
(Bloomington, IN: Indiana University Press, 1982) is an important study of apocalyptic fiction.
